The 17th Proof: Hadith of Anas on Tawfiq
Author presents a hadith proof and logical inference for tawfiq necessitating action.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the hadith of Anas and the logical inference from Allah's sufficiency of mentioning tawfiq prove that tawfiq necessitates righteous action, supporting the Ash'ari doctrine of kasb.

Core Idea
Tawfiq is not mere help; it necessitates the action.

This lesson examines the seventeenth proof for the Ash'ari position on divine predestination and human acquisition (kasb). Through a hadith narrated by Anas, the Prophet explains that when Allah desires good for a servant, He 'employs' him by granting him success (tawfiq) for righteous deeds. The author then draws a logical inference: Allah mentions only tawfiq, not the action itself, because tawfiq makes the action necessary. If the action could fail to occur despite tawfiq, Allah would have had to mention the action separately. This reasoning reinforces the idea that all actions are created by Allah and that the servant's role is acquisition.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith carefully
Read the Arabic text of the hadith from Anas and its translation. Notice the key term 'tawfiq'.
The hadith is short but dense.
2
Understand the definition of tawfiq
The author defines tawfiq as the preponderance of the motive for righteousness over the motive for corruption in the heart. This is a key concept.
Tawfiq is an act of Allah.
3
Follow the logical inference
The author argues that because Allah mentions only tawfiq and not the action itself, the action must necessarily follow from tawfiq. If it were possible for the action not to occur, mentioning tawfiq alone would be insufficient.
This is a conditional argument: if action could not follow, Allah would have mentioned it.
4
Connect to the Ash'ari doctrine
Understand how this proof supports the view that all actions are created by Allah and that human power (qudra) is effective through acquisition (kasb).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة السابعة عشر : ما روى أنس . أن النبي عليه السلام قال : ( إذا أراد الله بعبد خيراً ، استعمله ، قيل : فكيف يستعمله يا رسول الله ؟ قال : يوفقه لعمل صالح قبل الموت ) ووجه الاستدلال بهذا الخبر : هو أن هذا مذهبنا في أن قدرة العبد إن كانت صالحة للعمل الصالح وللعمل الفاسد . فذلك التوفيق ، عبارة عن ترجيح داعية الصلاح على داعية الفساد في قلبه . ثم إنه تعالى اكتفى بذكر هذا التوفيق عن وقوع ذلك العمل الصالح لأن عند حصول هذا التوفيق يكون حصول الفعل واجباً ، فاستغنى بذكر السبب عن ذكر المسبب . ولو كان تخلف الفعل عن حصول هذا التوفيق ممكناً ، لكان من الواجب أن لا يكتفي بذكر هذا التوفيق عن حصول ذلك الفعل . بل كان ينبغي أن يذكر أن ذلك الفعل . هل حصل أم لا ؟
The seventeenth proof: What Anas narrated, that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'If Allah desires good for a servant, He employs him.' It was said: 'How does He employ him, O Messenger of Allah?' He said: 'He grants him success (yuwaffiquhu) for righteous action before death.' And the aspect of inference from this report is that this is our doctrine—that the servant's power (qudra) is capable of both righteous action and corrupt action. So that success (tawfiq) is an expression of the preponderance of the motive for righteousness over the motive for corruption in his heart. Then He, exalted, sufficed with mentioning this success instead of the occurrence of that righteous action, because when this success occurs, the occurrence of the action becomes necessary, so He sufficed with mentioning the cause instead of mentioning the effect. And if the non-occurrence of the action despite the occurrence of this success were possible, it would have been necessary not to suffice with mentioning this success instead of the occurrence of that action. Rather, He should have mentioned whether that action occurred or not.
Source pages p. 237

Commentary
This passage presents the seventeenth proof for the Ash'ari doctrine of kasb and divine predestination. It is a scriptural proof (hadith) followed by a logical inference. The proof begins by citing the hadith where the Prophet says that when Allah wants good for a servant, He 'employs' him, which is explained as granting him success (tawfiq) for righteous deeds before death. The author then explains the inference: according to the Ash'ari school, the servant's power is capable of both good and evil. The tawfiq is the divine act of tipping the balance of motives in the heart towards righteousness. Allah mentions only tawfiq, not the action itself, because tawfiq necessarily leads to the action—the action is necessitated by the preponderant motive. If it were possible for the action not to occur despite tawfiq, then mentioning tawfiq alone would be insufficient; Allah would have had to specify whether the action actually occurred or not. The argument shows that the occurrence of the action is necessitated by tawfiq, supporting the Ash'ari view that all actions are created by Allah and that the servant's role is acquisition (kasb).

Key Terms
توفيق
داعية الصلاح
داعية الفساد
قدرة
وجوب
سبب
مسبب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think tawfiq is mere assistance that does not guarantee action.
Correction: The passage argues that tawfiq necessarily leads to action; otherwise, Allah would not have sufficed with mentioning it alone.

Checkpoint
According to the 17th proof, what does 'tawfiq' refer to?
A) The creation of the action by Allah
B) The servant's free choice
C) The preponderance of the motive for righteousness in the heart
D) The writing of destiny on the preserved tablet

Key Takeaway
The hadith and logical inference show that divine tawfiq necessitates righteous action, supporting the Ash'ari view that all actions are created by Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If tawfiq necessitates action, what does your failure to act righteously reveal about the state of your heart and the balance of your motives? Have you earnestly begged Allah to tip that balance, or do you rely on your own strength?
?
The hadith says tawfiq is granted before death. Are you living today as if you are expecting that tawfiq, actively seeking it through supplication and reliance on Allah, or are you assuming that your good deeds are from yourself?
?
When you find yourself procrastinating or neglecting a duty to Allah, pause and ask: have I truly been granted that preponderant motive from Allah? What concrete step will you take today to seek that divine success (tawfiq) before it is too late?

The 18th Proof: Hadith Qudsi on Creation for Paradise and Fire
Author cites a hadith qudsi and notes opponent's interpretation as foreknowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the hadith qudsi proof used in predestination debates and why opponents reinterpret it as referring to divine knowledge or the Preserved Tablet.

Core Idea
Divine creation for Paradise or Fire does not eliminate human responsibility; the hadith shows foreknowledge.

This lesson examines a short but significant proof from hadith qudsi. The author cites a well-known narration where Allah says He created some for Paradise and some for the Fire. Opponents reinterpret this as merely referring to Allah's knowledge or a written decree. The author notes that the complete refutation has already been given earlier, so our focus will be on understanding the proof and the objection.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the hadith qudsi and the opponent's interpretation mentioned.
The author does not repeat the earlier answer here, so we must rely on context.
2
Identify the core proof
The proof is the hadith itself: Allah directly creating people for their ultimate destiny. This implies that destiny is determined by divine creation, not solely by human choice.
3
Understand the opponent's response
Opponents claim the hadith refers to Allah's foreknowledge (علم) or the writing on the Preserved Tablet (اللوح المحفوظ), not actual causation.
This turns the proof into a statement of knowledge, not creation.
4
Reflect on the missing answer
The author says 'its answer has already preceded.' Think about what answer would reconcile divine creation with human responsibility—likely the distinction between creating based on foreknowledge and creating arbitrarily.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الثامنة عشر : قوله عليه السلام حكاية عن رب العزة : خلقت هؤلاء للجنة ولا أبالي وخلقت هؤلاء للنار ولا أبالي . والخصوم حملوه على العلم أو على الكتابة في اللوح المحفوظ . وقد سبق جوابه.
The eighteenth proof: His saying, peace be upon him, narrating from the Lord of Might: 'I created these for Paradise and I do not care, and I created these for the Fire and I do not care.' And the opponents interpreted it as [referring to] knowledge or as the writing on the Preserved Tablet. And its answer has already preceded.
Source pages p. 237

Commentary
This is a very brief proof that simply cites the well-known hadith qudsi indicating that Allah creates people directly for Paradise or the Fire, implying that their ultimate destiny is determined by divine creation, not by their own actions. The author notes that opponents (likely the Mu'tazila or Qadariyya) interpret this hadith as referring to Allah's foreknowledge or the decree written on the Preserved Tablet, thereby denying that the hadith proves predestination of people to bliss or perdition. The author states that the answer to those interpretations was already given earlier, so he does not repeat it here. This proof is thus a reference to a previous refutation.

Key Terms
رب العزة
علم
لوح محفوظ

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think this hadith proves that Allah arbitrarily creates people for heaven or hell regardless of their actions, thus denying free will and accountability.
Correction: The author's earlier answer (not repeated here) likely distinguishes between Allah's creative will and His legislative will, or shows that the hadith refers to the final outcome based on foreknowledge, not the creation of actions. Human responsibility remains intact.

Checkpoint
How do the opponents interpret the hadith 'I created these for Paradise...'?
A) As referring to actual creation of people for Paradise and Fire
B) As referring to Allah's knowledge or the writing on the Preserved Tablet
C) As a metaphor for the test of faith
D) As referring to the intercession of prophets

Key Takeaway
The hadith qudsi proof asserts divine creation for destiny, but opponents reinterpret it as foreknowledge, a refutation of which was already given earlier.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read that Allah created some for Paradise and some for Fire, does that make you feel a sense of urgency about your own state, or do you feel resigned? What does your emotional response reveal about your trust in Allah's justice and mercy?
?
The opponents reinterpreted the hadith as foreknowledge to avoid determinism. In your own life, do you sometimes use the concept of divine decree to excuse your sins or procrastinate on good deeds? How would your actions change if you truly believed that your choices matter despite Allah's foreknowledge?
?
The author does not repeat the refutation here but refers you back to an earlier answer. Are you willing to go back and study that answer, or are you content with a partial understanding? How does your diligence in seeking truth reflect your love for Allah?
